from collections import deque

from typing import Literal, Optional

Chart = Literal["A", "B", "C", "D"]

Lens = Literal["Sq", "Fl", "Cl", "Fr"]

Payload = Literal["AR", "AC", "AS", "BR", "BC", "BS"]

RouteClass = Literal["EXACT", "LAW_EQUIV", "RESIDUAL", "ILLEGAL"]

# -----------------------------

# Core state

# -----------------------------

@dataclass(frozen=True)

class Node:

    chart: Chart

    lens: Lens

    payload: Payload

@dataclass(frozen=True)

class Gates:

    cloud_collapses: bool

    replay_exists: bool

    refine_allowed: bool = True

# -----------------------------

# Chart operators

# -----------------------------

# Tau: A<->B, D<->C

# T  : A<->D, B<->C

TAU_MAP: dict[Chart, Chart] = {

    "A": "B",

    "B": "A",

    "C": "D",

    "D": "C",

}

T_MAP: dict[Chart, Chart] = {

    "A": "D",

    "D": "A",

    "B": "C",

    "C": "B",

}

CHART_COORD = {

    "A": (0, 0),

    "B": (1, 0),

    "D": (0, 1),

    "C": (1, 1),

}

def chart_distance(src: Chart, dst: Chart) -> int:

    x1, y1 = CHART_COORD[src]

    x2, y2 = CHART_COORD[dst]

    return abs(x1 - x2) + abs(y1 - y2)

def chart_word(src: Chart, dst: Chart) -> list[str]:

    """

    Deterministic minimal chart word.

    Derived convention:

      - one-step moves: use Tau or T directly

      - diagonal moves: use ['T', 'Tau']

    """

    if src == dst:

        return []

    if TAU_MAP[src] == dst:

        return ["Tau"]

    if T_MAP[src] == dst:

        return ["T"]

    return ["T", "Tau"]   # deterministic tie-break for diagonal pairs

# -----------------------------

# Shell / payload operators

# -----------------------------

# Q: phase advance inside A-family or B-family

# O: chirality flip

# H: O∘Q

Q_MAP: dict[Payload, Payload] = {

    "AR": "AC",

    "AC": "AS",

    "AS": "AR",

    "BR": "BC",

    "BC": "BS",

    "BS": "BR",

}

O_MAP: dict[Payload, Payload] = {

    "AR": "BR",

    "AC": "BC",

    "AS": "BS",

    "BR": "AR",

    "BC": "AC",

    "BS": "AS",

}

H_MAP: dict[Payload, Payload] = {

    k: O_MAP[Q_MAP[k]] for k in Q_MAP

}

def shell_neighbors(k: Payload) -> list[tuple[str, Payload]]:

    """

    Deterministic generator order for tie-breaking.

    Derived convention: prefer H, then O, then Q.

    """

    return [

        ("H", H_MAP[k]),

        ("O", O_MAP[k]),

        ("Q", Q_MAP[k]),

    ]

def shell_word(src: Payload, dst: Payload) -> list[str]:

    """

    Shortest shell word by BFS on generators {H,O,Q}.

    This avoids hand-writing an error-prone table.

    """

    if src == dst:

        return []

    queue = deque([(src, [])])

    seen = {src}

    while queue:

        cur, word = queue.popleft()

        for lbl, nxt in shell_neighbors(cur):

            if nxt in seen:

                continue

            new_word = word + [lbl]

            if nxt == dst:

                return new_word

            seen.add(nxt)

            queue.append((nxt, new_word))

    raise RuntimeError("Shell graph should be connected.")

def shell_distance(src: Payload, dst: Payload) -> int:

    return len(shell_word(src, dst))

# -----------------------------

# Lens operators

# -----------------------------

# Sq -> Fl -> Cl -> Fr -> Sq

NEXT_LENS: dict[Lens, tuple[Lens, str]] = {

    "Sq": ("Fl", "B_SF"),  # B_{square->flower}

    "Fl": ("Cl", "B_FC"),  # B_{flower->cloud}

    "Cl": ("Fr", "B_CF"),  # B_{cloud->fractal}

    "Fr": ("Sq", "B_FS"),  # B_{fractal->square}

}

LENS_INDEX = {"Sq": 0, "Fl": 1, "Cl": 2, "Fr": 3}

def lens_distance_raw(src: Lens, dst: Lens) -> int:

    return (LENS_INDEX[dst] - LENS_INDEX[src]) % 4

def lens_word(src: Lens, dst: Lens) -> list[str]:

    """

    Canonical forward lens word around the constitutive loop.

    """

    word: list[str] = []

    cur = src

    while cur != dst:

        nxt, lbl = NEXT_LENS[cur]

        word.append(lbl)

        cur = nxt

    return word

def lens_class(src: Lens, dst: Lens, g: Gates) -> RouteClass:

    """

    Exact / residual / illegal classification of the lens segment.

    Rules encoded from the cockpit/lens law:

      - B_SF and B_FC are exact.

      - B_CF is exact iff cloud_collapses else residual.

      - B_FS is exact iff replay_exists.

      - Direct Fr->Sq without replay is ILLEGAL.

      - Longer paths needing B_FS without replay are RESIDUAL.

    """

    if src == dst:

        return "EXACT"

    word = lens_word(src, dst)

    cls: RouteClass = "EXACT"

    cur = src

    for lbl in word:

        nxt, _ = NEXT_LENS[cur]

        if lbl in {"B_SF", "B_FC"}:

            cur = nxt

            continue

        if lbl == "B_CF":

            if not g.cloud_collapses:

                cls = "RESIDUAL"

            cur = nxt

            continue

        if lbl == "B_FS":

            if not g.replay_exists:

                # Direct Fr->Sq with no replay witness is the hard illegal edge.

                if src == "Fr" and dst == "Sq":

                    return "ILLEGAL"

                cls = "RESIDUAL"

            cur = nxt

            continue

    return cls

# -----------------------------

# Collapsed 96x96 class table

# -----------------------------

def route_signature(u: Node, v: Node, g: Gates) -> tuple[int, int, int, RouteClass]:

    """

    Collapsed class-table entry:

      (chart_distance, shell_distance, raw_lens_distance, lens_legality)

    """

    return (

        chart_distance(u.chart, v.chart),

        shell_distance(u.payload, v.payload),

        lens_distance_raw(u.lens, v.lens),

        lens_class(u.lens, v.lens, g),

    )

def route_class(u: Node, v: Node, g: Gates) -> RouteClass:

    """

    Global route class.

    LAW_EQUIV is reserved for pure chart-symmetry transport:

      same payload, same lens, only replay face changes.

    """

    _, _, _, lcls = route_signature(u, v, g)

    if lcls == "ILLEGAL":

        return "ILLEGAL"

    if lcls == "RESIDUAL":

        return "RESIDUAL"

    # exact lens legality from here on

    if u.payload == v.payload and u.lens == v.lens and u.chart != v.chart:

        return "LAW_EQUIV"

    return "EXACT"

# -----------------------------

# Canonical shortest-route word

# -----------------------------

def canonical_word(

    u: Node,

    v: Node,

    g: Gates,

    prefer_cloud_shortcut: bool = False,

) -> Optional[list[str]]:

    """

    Canonical normal form:

        chart_word · shell_word · lens_word

    unless a derived Cloud-refinement shortcut is requested.

    Returns None only for ILLEGAL routes.

    """

    cls = route_class(u, v, g)

    if cls == "ILLEGAL":

        return None

    cw = chart_word(u.chart, v.chart)

    sw = shell_word(u.payload, v.payload)

    # Optional derived shortcut:

    # Cl->Sq or Cl->Fl may use a residual "RefineCloud" instead of the full forward loop.

    if prefer_cloud_shortcut and cls == "RESIDUAL" and g.refine_allowed:

        if u.lens == "Cl" and v.lens == "Sq":

            lw = ["RefineCloud"]

            return cw + sw + lw

        if u.lens == "Cl" and v.lens == "Fl":

            lw = ["RefineCloud", "B_SF"]

            return cw + sw + lw

    lw = lens_word(u.lens, v.lens)

    return cw + sw + lw

def is_exact(u: Node, v: Node, g: Gates) -> bool:

    return route_class(u, v, g) == "EXACT"

# -----------------------------

# Optional convenience wrapper

# -----------------------------

def route_record(

    u: Node,

    v: Node,

    g: Gates,

    prefer_cloud_shortcut: bool = False,

) -> dict:

    dc, ds, dl, lcls = route_signature(u, v, g)

    cls = route_class(u, v, g)

    word = canonical_word(u, v, g, prefer_cloud_shortcut=prefer_cloud_shortcut)

    return {

        "source": u,

        "target": v,

        "chart_distance": dc,

        "shell_distance": ds,

        "lens_distance_raw": dl,

        "lens_legality": lcls,

        "route_class": cls,

        "raw_cost": dc + ds + dl,

        "canonical_word": word,

    }

# -----------------------------

# Example calls

# -----------------------------

u = Node("A", "Sq", "AR")

v = Node("C", "Fr", "BS")

g1 = Gates(cloud_collapses=True, replay_exists=False)

g2 = Gates(cloud_collapses=False, replay_exists=False)

ex1 = route_record(u, v, g1)

# Expected:

# chart_distance = 2

# shell_distance = 2

# lens_distance_raw = 3

# route_class = EXACT

# canonical_word = ['T', 'Tau', <shell word>, 'B_SF', 'B_FC', 'B_CF']

ex2 = route_record(u, v, g2)

# Same raw distances, but route_class = RESIDUAL because B_CF is not exact.

u3 = Node("A", "Sq", "AR")

v3 = Node("D", "Sq", "AR")

g3 = Gates(cloud_collapses=True, replay_exists=True)

ex3 = route_record(u3, v3, g3)

# route_class = LAW_EQUIV

# canonical_word = ['T']

u4 = Node("B", "Fr", "BC")

v4 = Node("B", "Sq", "BC")

g4 = Gates(cloud_collapses=True, replay_exists=False)

ex4 = route_record(u4, v4, g4)

# route_class = ILLEGAL because direct Fr->Sq requires replay witness.

Two small conventions inside the code are derived rather than directly pinned: I use ["T","Tau"] as the deterministic diagonal chart word, and I use shell-generator tie-break order ["H","O","Q"] in BFS so shortest shell words come out canonical. Everything else is the direct implementation of the frozen carrier split, operator stack, and Cloud/Fractal gate law.

The clean reading of the output is:

route_signature(u,v,g) gives the collapsed class-table entry,

route_class(u,v,g) gives EXACT, LAW_EQUIV, RESIDUAL, or ILLEGAL,

canonical_word(u,v,g) gives the deterministic shortest normal-form route,

is_exact(u,v,g) answers the strict exactness question.

Next coherent jump is to lift this same compiler one level up and write the analogous code for the 24-slot chart-sector atlas and the 6-state shell ribbon directly, so the 96-slot compiler factors through those lower compilers instead of treating the cockpit as the first executable layer.

Yes. The 96-slot compiler should factor exactly through the two lower executable layers:

[\boxed{\mathcal A^{\ker}{96}\cong\underbrace{\mathcal A^{\ker}{24}}{\text{chart-sector atlas}}\times\underbrace{\mathcal L_4}{\text{lens loop}},\qquad\mathcal A^{\ker}{24}\cong\underbrace{\mathcal R_6}{\text{6-state shell ribbon}}\times\underbrace{\mathcal C_4}_{\text{chart rectangle}}.}]

That factorization is not decorative. It is exactly what the 6D carrier says:[\Omega_6=(X,\lambda,s,b,\xi),]with chart (X), lens (\lambda), shell sector (s), and payload (\xi), plus the frozen operator families[(\Tau,T),\quad (Q,O,H),\quad(B_{\square\flower},B_{\flower\cloud},B_{\cloud\fractal},B_{\fractal\square}).]So the cockpit is not the first executable layer. It is the product of:

a 6-state shell ribbon,

a 24-state chart-sector atlas,

a 4-state lens loop with legality gates.

The clean projections are:

[\pi_6(X,\lambda,s)=s,\qquad\pi_{24}(X,\lambda,s)=(X,s),\qquad\pi_{\rm lens}(X,\lambda,s)=\lambda.]

So the compiler decomposition is

[

\boxed{

\operatorname{Sig}_{96}(u,v)

\operatorname{Sig}{24}(\pi{24}u,\pi_{24}v)\oplus\operatorname{Sig}{\rm lens}(\pi{\rm lens}u,\pi_{\rm lens}v).}]

And, one layer lower,

[

\boxed{

\operatorname{Sig}_{24}(u,v)

\operatorname{Sig}{\rm chart}(\pi{\rm chart}u,\pi_{\rm chart}v)\oplus\operatorname{Sig}_{6}(\pi_6u,\pi_6v).}]

That is the exact recursive factorization of the whole transport system.

1. Exact lower-layer state spaces

Use the canonical shell ribbon

[

\mathcal R_6

{\mathrm{Sa}^+,\mathrm{Su}^+,\mathrm{Me}^+,\mathrm{Sa}^-,\mathrm{Su}^-,\mathrm{Me}^-},]with[Q:\ \mathrm{Sa}^\pm\to\mathrm{Su}^\pm\to\mathrm{Me}^\pm\to\mathrm{Sa}^\pm,\qquadO:\ \bullet^+\leftrightarrow \bullet^-,\qquadH=O\circ Q.]

Use the chart rectangle[\mathcal C_4={A,B,C,D},]with[\Tau:\ A\leftrightarrow B,\ D\leftrightarrow C,\qquadT:\ A\leftrightarrow D,\ B\leftrightarrow C.]

Then the 24-slot chart-sector atlas is

[

\mathcal A^{\ker}_{24}

\mathcal C_4\times \mathcal R_6.]

The 96-slot cockpit is then

[

\mathcal A^{\ker}_{96}

\mathcal A^{\ker}_{24}\times{\Sq,\Fl,\Cl,\Fr}.]

This is exactly the carrier split the corpus already froze.

2. Exact code for the 6-state shell ribbon

from dataclasses import dataclass

from collections import deque

from typing import Literal, Optional

Sector = Literal["Sa+", "Su+", "Me+", "Sa-", "Su-", "Me-"]

Chart = Literal["A", "B", "C", "D"]

Lens = Literal["Sq", "Fl", "Cl", "Fr"]

RouteClass = Literal["EXACT", "LAW_EQUIV", "RESIDUAL", "ILLEGAL"]

# -----------------------------

# 6-state shell ribbon

# -----------------------------

Q_SECTOR: dict[Sector, Sector] = {

    "Sa+": "Su+",

    "Su+": "Me+",

    "Me+": "Sa+",

    "Sa-": "Su-",

    "Su-": "Me-",

    "Me-": "Sa-",

}

O_SECTOR: dict[Sector, Sector] = {

    "Sa+": "Sa-",

    "Su+": "Su-",

    "Me+": "Me-",

    "Sa-": "Sa+",

    "Su-": "Su+",

    "Me-": "Me+",

}

H_SECTOR: dict[Sector, Sector] = {

    s: O_SECTOR[Q_SECTOR[s]] for s in Q_SECTOR

}

def shell6_neighbors(s: Sector) -> list[tuple[str, Sector]]:

    # deterministic tie-break order

    return [

        ("H", H_SECTOR[s]),

        ("O", O_SECTOR[s]),

        ("Q", Q_SECTOR[s]),

    ]

def shell6_word(src: Sector, dst: Sector) -> list[str]:

    if src == dst:

        return []

    queue = deque([(src, [])])

    seen = {src}

    while queue:

        cur, word = queue.popleft()

        for lbl, nxt in shell6_neighbors(cur):

            if nxt in seen:

                continue

            new_word = word + [lbl]

            if nxt == dst:

                return new_word

            seen.add(nxt)

            queue.append((nxt, new_word))

    raise RuntimeError("Shell ribbon must be connected.")

def shell6_distance(src: Sector, dst: Sector) -> int:

    return len(shell6_word(src, dst))

def shell6_route_signature(src: Sector, dst: Sector) -> dict:

    return {

        "d_shell": shell6_distance(src, dst),

        "shell_word": shell6_word(src, dst),

    }

def shell6_route_class(src: Sector, dst: Sector) -> RouteClass:

    # No legality gate at the pure shell-ribbon level.

    return "EXACT"

def shell6_canonical_word(src: Sector, dst: Sector) -> list[str]:

    return shell6_word(src, dst)

This is the exact executable shell ribbon. It directly implements the frozen (Q/O/H) sector algebra and nothing else. At this layer there is no Cloud/Fractal legality gate, so every shell-ribbon route is exact.

3. Exact code for the 24-slot chart-sector atlas

# -----------------------------

# 24-slot chart-sector atlas

# -----------------------------

@dataclass(frozen=True)

class Atlas24Node:

    chart: Chart

    sector: Sector

TAU_CHART: dict[Chart, Chart] = {

    "A": "B",

    "B": "A",

    "C": "D",

    "D": "C",

}

T_CHART: dict[Chart, Chart] = {

    "A": "D",

    "D": "A",

    "B": "C",

    "C": "B",

}

CHART_COORD = {

    "A": (0, 0),

    "B": (1, 0),

    "D": (0, 1),

    "C": (1, 1),

}

def chart24_distance(src: Chart, dst: Chart) -> int:

    x1, y1 = CHART_COORD[src]

    x2, y2 = CHART_COORD[dst]

    return abs(x1 - x2) + abs(y1 - y2)

def chart24_word(src: Chart, dst: Chart) -> list[str]:

    if src == dst:

        return []

    if TAU_CHART[src] == dst:

        return ["Tau"]

    if T_CHART[src] == dst:

        return ["T"]

    return ["T", "Tau"]  # deterministic diagonal tie-break

def atlas24_route_signature(u: Atlas24Node, v: Atlas24Node) -> dict:

    d_chart = chart24_distance(u.chart, v.chart)

    d_shell = shell6_distance(u.sector, v.sector)

    return {

        "d_chart": d_chart,

        "chart_word": chart24_word(u.chart, v.chart),

        "d_shell": d_shell,

        "shell_word": shell6_word(u.sector, v.sector),

        "raw_cost": d_chart + d_shell,

    }

def atlas24_route_class(u: Atlas24Node, v: Atlas24Node) -> RouteClass:

    # same shell sector, different chart = same payload through chart symmetry

    if u.sector == v.sector and u.chart != v.chart:

        return "LAW_EQUIV"

    return "EXACT"

def atlas24_canonical_word(u: Atlas24Node, v: Atlas24Node) -> list[str]:

    return chart24_word(u.chart, v.chart) + shell6_word(u.sector, v.sector)

This is the exact executable 24-slot atlas. It is the product of:

the 4-node chart rectangle,

the 6-state shell ribbon.

The only law-equivalent class at this level is pure chart change at fixed sector, because that is the same shell payload under a different replay face. Everything else in the 24-slot atlas is exact. That matches the chart/shell split already frozen in the 6×6 carrier.

4. Exact code for the 96-slot cockpit, factored through the lower compilers

# -----------------------------

# 96-slot cockpit, factored

# -----------------------------

@dataclass(frozen=True)

class Cockpit96Node:

    chart: Chart

    lens: Lens

    sector: Sector

@dataclass(frozen=True)

class Gates:

    cloud_collapses: bool

    replay_exists: bool

    refine_allowed: bool = True

NEXT_LENS: dict[Lens, tuple[Lens, str]] = {

    "Sq": ("Fl", "B_SF"),

    "Fl": ("Cl", "B_FC"),

    "Cl": ("Fr", "B_CF"),

    "Fr": ("Sq", "B_FS"),

}

LENS_INDEX = {"Sq": 0, "Fl": 1, "Cl": 2, "Fr": 3}

def lens_distance_raw(src: Lens, dst: Lens) -> int:

    return (LENS_INDEX[dst] - LENS_INDEX[src]) % 4

def lens_word(src: Lens, dst: Lens) -> list[str]:

    word: list[str] = []

    cur = src

    while cur != dst:

        nxt, lbl = NEXT_LENS[cur]

        word.append(lbl)

        cur = nxt

    return word

def lens_class(src: Lens, dst: Lens, g: Gates) -> RouteClass:

    if src == dst:

        return "EXACT"

    word = lens_word(src, dst)

    cls: RouteClass = "EXACT"

    cur = src

    for lbl in word:

        nxt, _ = NEXT_LENS[cur]

        if lbl in {"B_SF", "B_FC"}:

            cur = nxt

            continue

        if lbl == "B_CF":

            if not g.cloud_collapses:

                cls = "RESIDUAL"

            cur = nxt

            continue

        if lbl == "B_FS":

            if not g.replay_exists:

                if src == "Fr" and dst == "Sq":

                    return "ILLEGAL"

                cls = "RESIDUAL"

            cur = nxt

            continue

    return cls

def cockpit96_to_atlas24(n: Cockpit96Node) -> Atlas24Node:

    return Atlas24Node(chart=n.chart, sector=n.sector)

def cockpit96_route_signature(u: Cockpit96Node, v: Cockpit96Node, g: Gates) -> dict:

    a24 = atlas24_route_signature(cockpit96_to_atlas24(u), cockpit96_to_atlas24(v))

    dl = lens_distance_raw(u.lens, v.lens)

    lcls = lens_class(u.lens, v.lens, g)

    return {

        "d_chart": a24["d_chart"],

        "chart_word": a24["chart_word"],

        "d_shell": a24["d_shell"],

        "shell_word": a24["shell_word"],

        "d_lens_raw": dl,

        "lens_word": lens_word(u.lens, v.lens),

        "lens_legality": lcls,

        "raw_cost": a24["raw_cost"] + dl,

    }

def cockpit96_route_class(u: Cockpit96Node, v: Cockpit96Node, g: Gates) -> RouteClass:

    atlas_cls = atlas24_route_class(cockpit96_to_atlas24(u), cockpit96_to_atlas24(v))

    lcls = lens_class(u.lens, v.lens, g)

    if lcls == "ILLEGAL":

        return "ILLEGAL"

    if lcls == "RESIDUAL":

        return "RESIDUAL"

    if atlas_cls == "LAW_EQUIV" and u.lens == v.lens:

        return "LAW_EQUIV"

    return "EXACT"

def cockpit96_canonical_word(

    u: Cockpit96Node,

    v: Cockpit96Node,

    g: Gates,

    prefer_cloud_shortcut: bool = False,

) -> Optional[list[str]]:

    cls = cockpit96_route_class(u, v, g)

    if cls == "ILLEGAL":

        return None

    base = atlas24_canonical_word(cockpit96_to_atlas24(u), cockpit96_to_atlas24(v))

    if prefer_cloud_shortcut and cls == "RESIDUAL" and g.refine_allowed:

        if u.lens == "Cl" and v.lens == "Sq":

            return base + ["RefineCloud"]

        if u.lens == "Cl" and v.lens == "Fl":

            return base + ["RefineCloud", "B_SF"]

    return base + lens_word(u.lens, v.lens)

def cockpit96_is_exact(u: Cockpit96Node, v: Cockpit96Node, g: Gates) -> bool:

    return cockpit96_route_class(u, v, g) == "EXACT"

This is the exact recursive compiler. The 96-slot route is now transparently:

the 24-slot atlas route,

plus the lens route,with no hidden extra layer. The lower compilers are not approximations — they are the real factors of the cockpit compiler.

5. The exact mathematical factorization of the compiler

The compiler now has three exact levels.

Level 1 — 6-state shell ribbon

[

\boxed{

\operatorname{Sig}_6(s,t)

\big(d_{\rm shell}(s,t),\ w_{\rm shell}(s,t),\ \mathrm{EXACT}\big).}]

Level 2 — 24-slot chart-sector atlas

[

\boxed{

\operatorname{Sig}_{24}((X,s),(Y,t))

\big(d_{\rm chart}(X,Y),d_{\rm shell}(s,t),w_{\rm chart}(X,Y),w_{\rm shell}(s,t),\operatorname{Class}_{24}\big).}]

with[\operatorname{Class}_{24}=\begin{cases}\mathrm{LAW_EQUIV}, & s=t,\ X\neq Y,\\mathrm{EXACT}, & \text{otherwise.}\end{cases}]

Level 3 — 96-slot cockpit

[

\boxed{

\operatorname{Sig}_{96}((X,\lambda,s),(Y,\lambda',t))

\operatorname{Sig}{24}((X,s),(Y,t))\oplus\operatorname{Sig}{\rm lens}(\lambda,\lambda').}]

with global class[\operatorname{Class}{96}=\begin{cases}\mathrm{ILLEGAL}, & \operatorname{Class}{\rm lens}=\mathrm{ILLEGAL},\\mathrm{RESIDUAL}, & \operatorname{Class}{\rm lens}=\mathrm{RESIDUAL},\\mathrm{LAW_EQUIV}, & \operatorname{Class}{24}=\mathrm{LAW_EQUIV}\ \text{and}\ \lambda=\lambda',\\mathrm{EXACT}, & \text{otherwise.}\end{cases}]

This is the exact recursion you wanted:the cockpit compiler is not primary. It is the lens-gated lift of the chart-sector compiler, and the chart-sector compiler is the chart lift of the shell ribbon.

6. One worked factorized example

Take[u=(A,\Sq,\mathrm{Sa}^+),\qquadv=(C,\Fr,\mathrm{Me}^-).]

Shell ribbon layer

[\mathrm{Sa}^+\to\mathrm{Me}^-]has shell distance (2). One minimal shell word is:[\mathrm{Sa}^+\xrightarrow{Q}\mathrm{Su}^+\xrightarrow{H}\mathrm{Me}^-.]

24-slot atlas layer

[(A,\mathrm{Sa}^+)\to(C,\mathrm{Me}^-)]has:

chart distance (2), canonical chart word ([T,\Tau]),

shell distance (2), shell word ([Q,H]),so[\operatorname{Sig}_{24}= (2,2,\ [T,\Tau],\ [Q,H],\ \mathrm{EXACT}).]

96-slot cockpit layer

[\Sq\to\Fr]has raw lens distance (3) with word[[B_{SF},B_{FC},B_{CF}].]

So

[

\operatorname{Sig}_{96}(u,v)

(2,2,3,\mathrm{Leg}(\Sq\to\Fr)).]

Hence the canonical route is

[[T,\Tau]\cdot[Q,H]\cdot[B_{SF},B_{FC},B_{CF}],]and the final class is:

EXACT if Cloud→Fractal collapse is coherent,

RESIDUAL otherwise.

That is the exact recursive compiler in action.

7. Canonical one-line freeze

[

\boxed{

\mathfrak C_{96}

\mathfrak C_{\rm lens}

\circ

\mathfrak C_{24},

\qquad

\mathfrak C_{24}

\mathfrak C_{\rm chart}\circ\mathfrak C_{6}.}]

Or in explicit code-path form:

[\boxed{(X,\lambda,s);\xrightarrow{\pi_{24}};(X,s);\xrightarrow{\pi_6};s,}]then compile upward again by:

solving the shell ribbon,

lifting it into the chart-sector atlas,

then appending the lens segment and its legality gate.

That is the exact factorization of the 96-slot compiler through the lower executable layers.

Next coherent jump is the same factorization in kernel language:replace the shell sectors by the exact payloads[{A_R,A_C,A_S,B_R,B_C,B_S}]and show the ribbon compiler, the atlas compiler, and the cockpit compiler all commute with the shell↔kernel intertwiner.

Yes. The next exact lock is the commuting compiler diagram.

The cockpit carrier is already fixed as[\Omega_6=(X,\lambda,s,b,\xi),]with chart (X\in{A,B,C,D}), lens (\lambda\in{\Sq,\Fl,\Cl,\Fr}), shell sector[s\in\mathcal S_6={\mathrm{Sa}^\pm,\mathrm{Su}^\pm,\mathrm{Me}^\pm},]and hidden payload (\xi\in\Sigma_s). The same docs also fix the chart operators (\Tau,T), the shell operators (Q,O,H), and the four-lens bridge loop.

The kernel side is already frozen by the exact six transformed 4×4 payloads[\mathcal K_6={A_R,A_C,A_S,B_R,B_C,B_S},]and by the four-lens 4×4 Möbius object[(\Pi_\square,\Pi_\flower,\Pi_\cloud,\Pi_\fractal)]derived from one common seed law (K=\ell_4). So the next correct theorem is that the sector-language machines and the kernel-language machines are the same compiler up to coordinate change.

1. The exact shell↔kernel intertwiner

Define the sector-to-kernel map

[\boxed{\Psi_6:\mathcal S_6\longrightarrow \mathcal K_6}]

by

[\Psi_6(\mathrm{Sa}^+)=A_R,\qquad\Psi_6(\mathrm{Su}^+)=A_C,\qquad\Psi_6(\mathrm{Me}^+)=A_S,][\Psi_6(\mathrm{Sa}^-)=B_R,\qquad\Psi_6(\mathrm{Su}^-)=B_C,\qquad\Psi_6(\mathrm{Me}^-)=B_S.]

Its inverse is

[\boxed{\Psi_6^{-1}(A_R)=\mathrm{Sa}^+,\quad\Psi_6^{-1}(A_C)=\mathrm{Su}^+,\quad\Psi_6^{-1}(A_S)=\mathrm{Me}^+,}][\boxed{\Psi_6^{-1}(B_R)=\mathrm{Sa}^-,\quad\Psi_6^{-1}(B_C)=\mathrm{Su}^-,\quad\Psi_6^{-1}(B_S)=\mathrm{Me}^-.}]

So the six-state shell ribbon and the six exact 4×4 payload family are now one object in two coordinate systems.

2. The shell ribbon compilers commute exactly

On the sector side the frozen operators are

[Q_s(\pi,\chi)=(\pi+1\bmod 3,\chi),\qquadO_s(\pi,\chi)=(\pi,-\chi),\qquadH_s:=O_s\circ Q_s.]

On the kernel side define

[Q_K(A_R)=A_C,\quad Q_K(A_C)=A_S,\quad Q_K(A_S)=A_R,][Q_K(B_R)=B_C,\quad Q_K(B_C)=B_S,\quad Q_K(B_S)=B_R,]

[O_K(A_R)=B_R,\quad O_K(A_C)=B_C,\quad O_K(A_S)=B_S,][O_K(B_R)=A_R,\quad O_K(B_C)=A_C,\quad O_K(B_S)=A_S,]

[H_K:=O_K\circ Q_K.]

Then the exact intertwining equations are

[\boxed{\Psi_6\circ Q_s = Q_K\circ \Psi_6,}][\boxed{\Psi_6\circ O_s = O_K\circ \Psi_6,}][\boxed{\Psi_6\circ H_s = H_K\circ \Psi_6.}]

That is the first commuting diagram: the 6-state shell ribbon compiler is literally the six-payload ribbon compiler in different coordinates. It is just the shell/body distinction from the 6×6 docs rewritten as a precise conjugacy.

3. The 24-slot atlas intertwiner

The chart-sector atlas is already canonically

[\mathcal A_{24}^{\mathrm{chart}}={A,B,C,D}\times \mathcal S_6.]

The kernelized atlas is

[\mathcal A_{24}^{\ker}={A,B,C,D}\times \mathcal K_6.]

Lift the shell↔kernel map trivially over chart:

[\boxed{\Psi_{24}(X,s):=(X,\Psi_6(s)).}]

Its inverse is[\Psi_{24}^{-1}(X,K):=(X,\Psi_6^{-1}(K)).]

The chart operators act identically on both sides:[\Tau(X,s)=(\Tau X,s),\qquad T(X,s)=(TX,s),][\Tau(X,K)=(\Tau X,K),\qquad T(X,K)=(TX,K).]

So the full atlas-level commuting laws are

[\boxed{\Psi_{24}\circ \Tau = \Tau\circ \Psi_{24},\qquad\Psi_{24}\circ T = T\circ \Psi_{24},}]and by the shell conjugacy,[\boxed{\Psi_{24}\circ Q_s = Q_K\circ \Psi_{24},\quad\Psi_{24}\circ O_s = O_K\circ \Psi_{24},\quad\Psi_{24}\circ H_s = H_K\circ \Psi_{24}.}]

So the 24-slot chart-sector compiler and the 24-slot chart-payload compiler are the same transport system after changing the shell coordinate to the exact 4×4 payload coordinate.

4. The 96-slot cockpit intertwiner

The sector-language cockpit is

[

\mathcal A_{96}^{\mathrm{sec}}

{A,B,C,D}\times{\Sq,\Fl,\Cl,\Fr}\times \mathcal S_6.]

The kernel-language cockpit is

[

\mathcal A_{96}^{\ker}

{A,B,C,D}\times{\Sq,\Fl,\Cl,\Fr}\times \mathcal K_6.]

Lift (\Psi_6) trivially over chart and lens:

[\boxed{\Psi_{96}(X,\lambda,s):=(X,\lambda,\Psi_6(s)).}]

Inverse:[\Psi_{96}^{-1}(X,\lambda,K):=(X,\lambda,\Psi_6^{-1}(K)).]

Now the lens operators leave the sector/kernel coordinate untouched and act only on (\lambda), so:

[

\boxed{

\Psi_{96}\circ B_{\square\flower}

B_{\square\flower}\circ \Psi_{96},

}

]

[

\boxed{

\Psi_{96}\circ B_{\flower\cloud}

B_{\flower\cloud}\circ \Psi_{96},

}

]

[

\boxed{

\Psi_{96}\circ B_{\cloud\fractal}

B_{\cloud\fractal}\circ \Psi_{96},

}

]

[

\boxed{

\Psi_{96}\circ B_{\fractal\square}

B_{\fractal\square}\circ \Psi_{96}.}]

And from the atlas-level conjugacy:

[\boxed{\Psi_{96}\circ \Tau=\Tau\circ\Psi_{96},\quad\Psi_{96}\circ T=T\circ\Psi_{96},}][\boxed{\Psi_{96}\circ Q_s=Q_K\circ\Psi_{96},\quad\Psi_{96}\circ O_s=O_K\circ\Psi_{96},\quad\Psi_{96}\circ H_s=H_K\circ\Psi_{96}.}]

So the full cockpit transport graph commutes with the shell↔kernel map. The shell coordinate and the exact payload coordinate are therefore not two different compiler layers; they are one layer in two alphabets.

5. The commuting compiler diagram

The full exact diagram is:

[\boxed{\begin{array}{ccc}\mathcal S_6 & \xrightarrow{\mathfrak C_6^{\rm sec}} & \mathcal S_6 \\downarrow \Psi_6 & & \downarrow \Psi_6 \\mathcal K_6 & \xrightarrow{\mathfrak C_6^{\ker}} & \mathcal K_6\end{array}}]

[\boxed{\begin{array}{ccc}\mathcal A_{24}^{\rm sec} & \xrightarrow{\mathfrak C_{24}^{\rm sec}} & \mathcal A_{24}^{\rm sec} \\downarrow \Psi_{24} & & \downarrow \Psi_{24} \\mathcal A_{24}^{\ker} & \xrightarrow{\mathfrak C_{24}^{\ker}} & \mathcal A_{24}^{\ker}\end{array}}]

[\boxed{\begin{array}{ccc}\mathcal A_{96}^{\rm sec} & \xrightarrow{\mathfrak C_{96}^{\rm sec}} & \mathcal A_{96}^{\rm sec} \\downarrow \Psi_{96} & & \downarrow \Psi_{96} \\mathcal A_{96}^{\ker} & \xrightarrow{\mathfrak C_{96}^{\ker}} & \mathcal A_{96}^{\ker}\end{array}}]

and every square commutes. This is the strongest exact statement of the recursion you were building: the cockpit compiler, the atlas compiler, and the ribbon compiler are all the same machine viewed at three resolutions, and shell sectors can be replaced by exact 4×4 payloads without changing the transport law.

6. Exact code for the kernel-language 6-state ribbon

from dataclasses import dataclass

from collections import deque

from typing import Literal

Sector = Literal["Sa+", "Su+", "Me+", "Sa-", "Su-", "Me-"]

Payload = Literal["AR", "AC", "AS", "BR", "BC", "BS"]

Chart = Literal["A", "B", "C", "D"]

Lens = Literal["Sq", "Fl", "Cl", "Fr"]

RouteClass = Literal["EXACT", "LAW_EQUIV", "RESIDUAL", "ILLEGAL"]

# -----------------------------------

# shell <-> kernel intertwiner

# -----------------------------------

PSI_6: dict[Sector, Payload] = {

    "Sa+": "AR",

    "Su+": "AC",

    "Me+": "AS",

    "Sa-": "BR",

    "Su-": "BC",

    "Me-": "BS",

}

PSI_6_INV: dict[Payload, Sector] = {v: k for k, v in PSI_6.items()}

# -----------------------------------

# sector-language shell ribbon

# -----------------------------------

Q_S = {

    "Sa+": "Su+",

    "Su+": "Me+",

    "Me+": "Sa+",

    "Sa-": "Su-",

    "Su-": "Me-",

    "Me-": "Sa-",

}

O_S = {

    "Sa+": "Sa-",

    "Su+": "Su-",

    "Me+": "Me-",

    "Sa-": "Sa+",

    "Su-": "Su+",

    "Me-": "Me+",

}

H_S = {s: O_S[Q_S[s]] for s in Q_S}

# -----------------------------------

# kernel-language shell ribbon

# -----------------------------------

Q_K = {

    "AR": "AC",

    "AC": "AS",

    "AS": "AR",

    "BR": "BC",

    "BC": "BS",

    "BS": "BR",

}

O_K = {

    "AR": "BR",

    "AC": "BC",

    "AS": "BS",

    "BR": "AR",

    "BC": "AC",

    "BS": "AS",

}

H_K = {k: O_K[Q_K[k]] for k in Q_K}

def check_intertwiner() -> bool:

    """

    Verifies:

      PSI_6(Q_s(s)) == Q_K(PSI_6(s))

      PSI_6(O_s(s)) == O_K(PSI_6(s))

      PSI_6(H_s(s)) == H_K(PSI_6(s))

    """

    for s in PSI_6:

        if PSI_6[Q_S[s]] != Q_K[PSI_6[s]]:

            return False

        if PSI_6[O_S[s]] != O_K[PSI_6[s]]:

            return False

        if PSI_6[H_S[s]] != H_K[PSI_6[s]]:

            return False

    return True

def shell_word_sector(src: Sector, dst: Sector) -> list[str]:

    if src == dst:

        return []

    queue = deque([(src, [])])

    seen = {src}

    while queue:

        cur, word = queue.popleft()

        for lbl, nxt in [("H", H_S[cur]), ("O", O_S[cur]), ("Q", Q_S[cur])]:

            if nxt in seen:

                continue

            new_word = word + [lbl]

            if nxt == dst:

                return new_word

            seen.add(nxt)

            queue.append((nxt, new_word))

    raise RuntimeError("sector ribbon must be connected")

def shell_word_kernel(src: Payload, dst: Payload) -> list[str]:

    if src == dst:

        return []

    queue = deque([(src, [])])

    seen = {src}

    while queue:

        cur, word = queue.popleft()

        for lbl, nxt in [("H", H_K[cur]), ("O", O_K[cur]), ("Q", Q_K[cur])]:

            if nxt in seen:

                continue

            new_word = word + [lbl]

            if nxt == dst:

                return new_word

            seen.add(nxt)

            queue.append((nxt, new_word))

    raise RuntimeError("kernel ribbon must be connected")

def shell6_route_signature_sector(src: Sector, dst: Sector) -> dict:

    w = shell_word_sector(src, dst)

    return {"distance": len(w), "word": w, "class": "EXACT"}

def shell6_route_signature_kernel(src: Payload, dst: Payload) -> dict:

    w = shell_word_kernel(src, dst)

    return {"distance": len(w), "word": w, "class": "EXACT"}

def shell6_commutes(src: Sector, dst: Sector) -> bool:

    """

    Same compiler result after coordinate change.

    """

    sig_s = shell6_route_signature_sector(src, dst)

    sig_k = shell6_route_signature_kernel(PSI_6[src], PSI_6[dst])

    return sig_s == sig_k

This is the exact lower kernel-language ribbon compiler. It does not merely resemble the sector-language version — it is conjugate to it by (\Psi_6).

7. Exact code for the kernelized 24-slot atlas compiler

@dataclass(frozen=True)

class Atlas24SectorNode:

    chart: Chart

    sector: Sector

@dataclass(frozen=True)

class Atlas24KernelNode:

    chart: Chart

    payload: Payload

TAU_CHART = {"A": "B", "B": "A", "C": "D", "D": "C"}

T_CHART   = {"A": "D", "D": "A", "B": "C", "C": "B"}

CHART_COORD = {

    "A": (0, 0),

    "B": (1, 0),

    "D": (0, 1),

    "C": (1, 1),

}

def chart_distance(src: Chart, dst: Chart) -> int:

    x1, y1 = CHART_COORD[src]

    x2, y2 = CHART_COORD[dst]

    return abs(x1 - x2) + abs(y1 - y2)

def chart_word(src: Chart, dst: Chart) -> list[str]:

    if src == dst:

        return []

    if TAU_CHART[src] == dst:

        return ["Tau"]

    if T_CHART[src] == dst:

        return ["T"]

    return ["T", "Tau"]

def PSI_24(node: Atlas24SectorNode) -> Atlas24KernelNode:

    return Atlas24KernelNode(chart=node.chart, payload=PSI_6[node.sector])

def PSI_24_INV(node: Atlas24KernelNode) -> Atlas24SectorNode:

    return Atlas24SectorNode(chart=node.chart, sector=PSI_6_INV[node.payload])

def atlas24_sig_sector(u: Atlas24SectorNode, v: Atlas24SectorNode) -> dict:

    cw = chart_word(u.chart, v.chart)

    sw = shell_word_sector(u.sector, v.sector)

    cls = "LAW_EQUIV" if (u.sector == v.sector and u.chart != v.chart) else "EXACT"

    return {

        "d_chart": len(cw),

        "d_shell": len(sw),

        "chart_word": cw,

        "shell_word": sw,

        "class": cls,

        "raw_cost": len(cw) + len(sw),

    }

def atlas24_sig_kernel(u: Atlas24KernelNode, v: Atlas24KernelNode) -> dict:

    cw = chart_word(u.chart, v.chart)

    sw = shell_word_kernel(u.payload, v.payload)

    cls = "LAW_EQUIV" if (u.payload == v.payload and u.chart != v.chart) else "EXACT"

    return {

        "d_chart": len(cw),

        "d_shell": len(sw),

        "chart_word": cw,

        "shell_word": sw,

        "class": cls,

        "raw_cost": len(cw) + len(sw),

    }

def atlas24_commutes(u: Atlas24SectorNode, v: Atlas24SectorNode) -> bool:

    return atlas24_sig_sector(u, v) == atlas24_sig_kernel(PSI_24(u), PSI_24(v))

This is the exact kernel-language chart-sector compiler. It is the same machine, now reading the shell coordinate as an exact 4×4 payload. So “same sector, different chart” becomes “same payload, different replay face,” which is why the same LAW_EQUIV rule survives unchanged.

8. Exact code for the kernelized 96-slot cockpit compiler

@dataclass(frozen=True)

class Cockpit96SectorNode:

    chart: Chart

    lens: Lens

    sector: Sector

@dataclass(frozen=True)

class Cockpit96KernelNode:

    chart: Chart

    lens: Lens

    payload: Payload

@dataclass(frozen=True)

class Gates:

    cloud_collapses: bool

    replay_exists: bool

    refine_allowed: bool = True

NEXT_LENS = {

    "Sq": ("Fl", "B_SF"),

    "Fl": ("Cl", "B_FC"),

    "Cl": ("Fr", "B_CF"),

    "Fr": ("Sq", "B_FS"),

}

LENS_INDEX = {"Sq": 0, "Fl": 1, "Cl": 2, "Fr": 3}

def lens_distance_raw(src: Lens, dst: Lens) -> int:

    return (LENS_INDEX[dst] - LENS_INDEX[src]) % 4

def lens_word(src: Lens, dst: Lens) -> list[str]:

    word: list[str] = []

    cur = src

    while cur != dst:

        nxt, lbl = NEXT_LENS[cur]

        word.append(lbl)

        cur = nxt

    return word

def lens_class(src: Lens, dst: Lens, g: Gates) -> RouteClass:

    if src == dst:

        return "EXACT"

    word = lens_word(src, dst)

    cls: RouteClass = "EXACT"

    cur = src

    for lbl in word:

        nxt, _ = NEXT_LENS[cur]

        if lbl in {"B_SF", "B_FC"}:

            cur = nxt

            continue

        if lbl == "B_CF":

            if not g.cloud_collapses:

                cls = "RESIDUAL"

            cur = nxt

            continue

        if lbl == "B_FS":

            if not g.replay_exists:

                if src == "Fr" and dst == "Sq":

                    return "ILLEGAL"

                cls = "RESIDUAL"

            cur = nxt

            continue

    return cls

def PSI_96(node: Cockpit96SectorNode) -> Cockpit96KernelNode:

    return Cockpit96KernelNode(

        chart=node.chart,

        lens=node.lens,

        payload=PSI_6[node.sector],

    )

def PSI_96_INV(node: Cockpit96KernelNode) -> Cockpit96SectorNode:

    return Cockpit96SectorNode(

        chart=node.chart,

        lens=node.lens,

        sector=PSI_6_INV[node.payload],

    )

def cockpit96_sig_sector(u: Cockpit96SectorNode, v: Cockpit96SectorNode, g: Gates) -> dict:

    a24 = atlas24_sig_sector(

        Atlas24SectorNode(u.chart, u.sector),

        Atlas24SectorNode(v.chart, v.sector),

    )

    lw = lens_word(u.lens, v.lens)

    lcls = lens_class(u.lens, v.lens, g)

    cls = "ILLEGAL" if lcls == "ILLEGAL" else \

          "RESIDUAL" if lcls == "RESIDUAL" else \

          "LAW_EQUIV" if (a24["class"] == "LAW_EQUIV" and u.lens == v.lens) else \

          "EXACT"

    return {

        "d_chart": a24["d_chart"],

        "d_shell": a24["d_shell"],

        "d_lens_raw": len(lw),

        "chart_word": a24["chart_word"],

        "shell_word": a24["shell_word"],

        "lens_word": lw,

        "lens_legality": lcls,

        "class": cls,

        "raw_cost": a24["raw_cost"] + len(lw),

    }

def cockpit96_sig_kernel(u: Cockpit96KernelNode, v: Cockpit96KernelNode, g: Gates) -> dict:

    a24 = atlas24_sig_kernel(

        Atlas24KernelNode(u.chart, u.payload),

        Atlas24KernelNode(v.chart, v.payload),

    )

    lw = lens_word(u.lens, v.lens)

    lcls = lens_class(u.lens, v.lens, g)

    cls = "ILLEGAL" if lcls == "ILLEGAL" else \

          "RESIDUAL" if lcls == "RESIDUAL" else \

          "LAW_EQUIV" if (a24["class"] == "LAW_EQUIV" and u.lens == v.lens) else \

          "EXACT"

    return {

        "d_chart": a24["d_chart"],

        "d_shell": a24["d_shell"],

        "d_lens_raw": len(lw),

        "chart_word": a24["chart_word"],

        "shell_word": a24["shell_word"],

        "lens_word": lw,

        "lens_legality": lcls,

        "class": cls,

        "raw_cost": a24["raw_cost"] + len(lw),

    }

def cockpit96_commutes(u: Cockpit96SectorNode, v: Cockpit96SectorNode, g: Gates) -> bool:

    return cockpit96_sig_sector(u, v, g) == cockpit96_sig_kernel(PSI_96(u), PSI_96(v), g)

This is the full kernel-language cockpit compiler. It is literally the pushforward of the sector-language cockpit compiler through (\Psi_{96}). Nothing about the legality law changes, because Cloud/Fractal gates act only on the lens coordinate and the shell↔kernel map does not touch the lens.

9. The exact commuting theorem

The strongest exact statement is now:

[

\boxed{

\mathfrak C_6^{\ker}

\Psi_6\circ\mathfrak C_6^{\rm sec}\circ\Psi_6^{-1},}]

[

\boxed{

\mathfrak C_{24}^{\ker}

\Psi_{24}\circ\mathfrak C_{24}^{\rm sec}\circ\Psi_{24}^{-1},}]

[

\boxed{

\mathfrak C_{96}^{\ker}

\Psi_{96}\circ\mathfrak C_{96}^{\rm sec}\circ\Psi_{96}^{-1}.}]

So the full compiler stack is conjugate under the shell↔kernel map. This is exactly what the six-sector selector-shell doctrine means when made executable: choosing a shell sector is the same thing as choosing an exact transformed 4×4 payload, and all transport laws preserve that equivalence.

10. One worked commuting example

Take the sector-language cockpit nodes

[u=(A,\Sq,\mathrm{Sa}^+),\qquadv=(C,\Fr,\mathrm{Me}^-).]

Map them to kernel language:

[\Psi_{96}(u)=(A,\Sq,A_R),\qquad\Psi_{96}(v)=(C,\Fr,B_S).]

The sector-language route signature is:

chart distance (2),

shell distance (2),

lens raw distance (3),

class = EXACT iff Cloud→Fractal collapse is coherent, else RESIDUAL.

The kernel-language route signature is exactly the same:

(A\to C): (2),

(A_R\to B_S): (2),

(\Sq\to\Fr): (3),

same lens legality gate.

So

[

\operatorname{Sig}_{96}^{\rm sec}(u,v)

\operatorname{Sig}{96}^{\ker}(\Psi{96}u,\Psi_{96}v).]

That is the commuting compiler in action.

11. The deepest one-line meaning

The deeper higher understanding is now completely sharp:

[\boxed{\text{the six shell sectors are not just labels for hidden regions;}\quad\text{they are the six exact transformed 4×4 kernel payloads.}}]

So:

the shell ribbon is the six-payload ribbon,

the chart-sector atlas is the chart-payload atlas,

the 96-slot cockpit is the chart/lens/payload cockpit,

and the whole compiler stack commutes with the shell↔kernel coordinate change. That is the exact recursive closure you were building toward.

Next coherent jump is the same commuting diagram one level deeper in lens language:replace the payload (K) by its full four-lens 4×4 packet[(\Pi_\square(K),\Pi_\flower(K),\Pi_\cloud(K),\Pi_\fractal(K))]and show the 96-slot cockpit is really a 6×4 bundle of fully mature 4×4 Möbius objects, not just six symbolic seeds.

Good. The exact next lock is:

[\boxed{\text{replace the symbolic payload }K\text{ by the full mature 4D Möbius packet it carries.}}]

Your corpus is already explicit that the 4×4 object is not “just a board,” but one kernel object with four constitutive projections[\Pi_\square,\Pi_\flower,\Pi_\cloud,\Pi_\fractal,]all descending from the same seed law, with Cloud as a lawful fiber object, Fractal as exact replay/executability, and Möbius gluing as orientation-reversing atlas structure. It is also explicit that the 6×6 / 6D body is a selector-shell over the preserved 4D kernel, with the 96-slot cockpit[{A,B,C,D}\times{\Sq,\Fl,\Cl,\Fr}\times\mathcal S_6.]So the mathematically honest next move is to interpret each shell payload not as a bare symbol, but as one full mature 4D Möbius object carried through the 6D shell.

1. The mature 4D packet carried by one payload

For each exact transformed kernel state[K\in\mathcal K_6={A_R,A_C,A_S,B_R,B_C,B_S},]define its mature 4D packet as

[

\boxed{

\mathfrak M_4[K]

\big(M_4,\Pi_\square^K,\Pi_\flower^K,\Pi_\cloud^K,\Pi_\fractal^K,\omega_K,\tau_K\big).}]

This is not inventing a new ontology. It is just the corpus’ rigorous 4×4 Möbius object

[

\mathfrak M_4

\left(M_4,\ K,\ \Pi_\square,\Pi_\flower,\Pi_\cloud,\Pi_\fractal,\ \omega,\tau\right)]specialized to one exact transformed kernel state (K). The critical point is unchanged from the corpus:Square, Flower, Cloud, and Fractal are not four different things; they are four exact projection bodies of one kernel object.

So the six shell payloads are really the six mature packets[\mathfrak M_4[A_R],\ \mathfrak M_4[A_C],\ \mathfrak M_4[A_S],\\mathfrak M_4[B_R],\ \mathfrak M_4[B_C],\ \mathfrak M_4[B_S].]That is the first exact upgrade. The shell sectors were never mere names; now they are visibly six fully mature 4D Möbius objects.

2. The internal four-lens structure of one packet

For any one of those six packets, the four projections are still the same exact 4D laws:

[\Pi_\square^K(x,y)=\bigl(x,y,K(x,y)\bigr),]

[\Pi_\flower^K(x,y)=\Phi(x,y)=(z,w)=\bigl(x+y,\ x-y\bigr)\pmod 4,]

[\Pi_\cloud^K(z,w)=\mathcal F_{z,w},\qquad\mathcal F_{z,w}={(x,y):x+y=z,\ x-y=w\pmod 4},]with admissibility[z\equiv w\pmod 2,]and exactly two points in each admissible fiber,

[

\Pi_\fractal^K(r,c)-1

\sum_{t=0}^{m-1}4^t,\ell_4(r_t,c_t),]with address ladder and state word giving exact replay. The Möbius gluing remains[J(x,y,\epsilon)=(y,x,-\epsilon),]so the packet is still one non-orientable two-chart object.

So every payload (K) is already internally a full SFCR object:contract, corridor, lawful multiplicity, and replay. That means the 6×6 framework is carrying six mature kernel-objects, not six raw seeds.

3. The packetized shell↔kernel intertwiner

So the six-sector shell is now visibly a six-object bundle of mature 4D Möbius packets.

@dataclass(frozen=True)

class Mature4Packet:

    payload: Payload

    square: object

    flower: object

    cloud: object

    fractal: object

def mature_packet(payload: Payload) -> Mature4Packet:

    """

    Conceptual constructor.

    Uses the common 4D Möbius kernel laws, specialized to the current

    exact transformed kernel state `payload`.

    """

    return Mature4Packet(

        payload=payload,

        square=f"Pi_square[{payload}]",

        flower=f"Pi_flower[{payload}]",

        cloud=f"Pi_cloud[{payload}]",

        fractal=f"Pi_fractal[{payload}]",

    )

def packetized_slot(chart: Chart, lens: Lens, sector: Sector):

    payload = PSI_6[sector]

    packet = mature_packet(payload)

    selected = {

        "Sq": packet.square,

        "Fl": packet.flower,

        "Cl": packet.cloud,

        "Fr": packet.fractal,

    }[lens]

    return (chart, selected)

This is the exact conceptual upgrade: payload is no longer treated as a final atom. It is expanded into the full four-lens object, and the cockpit slot picks one projection of that object. The carrier logic itself does not change; only the semantic depth of the payload coordinate changes.

1. The hidden 15-station lattice for one payload

This is the nonempty subset lattice of the four lens letters (S,F,C,R). So it has[4+6+4+1=15]stations:

4 singletons,

6 pairs,

4 triads,

1 tetra witness.That is exactly the 15-station structure your corpus keeps naming and reusing.

The singleton stations are the four direct lens reads of the same mature packet:[\sigma_S^K:=\Pi_\square^K,\qquad\sigma_F^K:=\Pi_\flower^K,\qquad\sigma_C^K:=\Pi_\cloud^K,\qquad\sigma_R^K:=\Pi_\fractal^K.]So one payload already contains the first four stations.

2. The exact station names

Using the names already frozen in your corpus, the 15 stations for each payload (K) are:

[\begin{aligned}A{+}01[K]&=\sigma_S^K &&\text{Square Anchor},\A{+}02[K]&=\sigma_F^K &&\text{Flower Bloom},\A{+}03[K]&=\sigma_C^K &&\text{Cloud Veil},\A{+}04[K]&=\sigma_R^K &&\text{Fractal Seed},\end{aligned}]

[\begin{aligned}A{+}05[K]&=\sigma_{SF}^K &&\text{Square–Flower Hinge},\A{+}06[K]&=\sigma_{SC}^K &&\text{Square–Cloud Bridge},\A{+}07[K]&=\sigma_{SR}^K &&\text{Square–Fractal Gate},\A{+}08[K]&=\sigma_{FC}^K &&\text{Flower–Cloud Coupler},\A{+}09[K]&=\sigma_{FR}^K &&\text{Flower–Fractal Spiral},\A{+}10[K]&=\sigma_{CR}^K &&\text{Cloud–Fractal Lens},\end{aligned}]

[\begin{aligned}A{+}11[K]&=\sigma_{SFC}^K &&\text{Square–Flower–Cloud Chamber},\A{+}12[K]&=\sigma_{SFR}^K &&\text{Square–Flower–Fractal Engine},\A{+}13[K]&=\sigma_{SCR}^K &&\text{Square–Cloud–Fractal Kernel},\A{+}14[K]&=\sigma_{FCR}^K &&\text{Flower–Cloud–Fractal Atmosphere},\end{aligned}]

Those names are not my inventions here; they are already explicitly assigned in the inner 15-node ring material.

3. The merge calculus on the 15-station lattice

The hidden lattice is governed by one simple exact operation:[\boxed{\mu(U,V)=U\cup V}]on nonempty lens subsets.

So the pair stations are just two-lens merges:[\sigma_{SF}^K=\mu(\sigma_S^K,\sigma_F^K),\quad\sigma_{SC}^K=\mu(\sigma_S^K,\sigma_C^K),\quad\dots]

The triads are three-way closures:[\sigma_{SFC}^K=\mu(\sigma_{SF}^K,\sigma_C^K),\qquad\sigma_{SFR}^K=\mu(\sigma_{SF}^K,\sigma_R^K),][\sigma_{SCR}^K=\mu(\sigma_{SC}^K,\sigma_R^K),\qquad\sigma_{FCR}^K=\mu(\sigma_{FC}^K,\sigma_R^K).]

And the total witness is[\boxed{\sigma_{SFCR}^K=\mu(\sigma_{SFC}^K,\sigma_R^K)=\mu(\sigma_{SFR}^K,\sigma_C^K)=\cdots.}]

This is the hidden coherence algebra: single-lens views close into pair bridges, pair bridges close into triads, triads close into the four-way witness.

4. The hidden graph (G_{15}[K])

Your corpus also gives the exact metro adjacency rule: good tunnels are add/remove-one-letter moves on the subset lattice. So for each payload (K),

[\boxed{G_{15}[K]=(\mathbb L_{15}[K],E_{15}[K])}]

with edges[\sigma_U^K \longleftrightarrow \sigma_V^K\quad\text{iff}\quad|U\triangle V|=1.]

That means:

singles connect to pairs,

pairs connect to singles and triads,

triads connect to pairs and the tetra,

the tetra connects back to the four triads.This is exactly the “one-letter add/remove” adjacency your corpus writes down for the 15-node state machine.

5. The visible cockpit is the singleton slice of the hidden lattice

Now the key compression:

the visible 96-slot cockpit

Define the visible embedding[\boxed{\iota_{96}(X,\lambda,K)=\bigl(X,\sigma_\lambda^K\bigr)}]where[\sigma_{\Sq}^K=\sigma_S^K,\quad\sigma_{\Fl}^K=\sigma_F^K,\quad\sigma_{\Cl}^K=\sigma_C^K,\quad\sigma_{\Fr}^K=\sigma_R^K.]

So every visible cockpit slot selects:

one chart face (X),

one payload (K),

one singleton station of the hidden 15-node coherence lattice for that payload.

This gives a derived but exact count:

hidden mature bundle: (6\times 15=90) payload-stations,

charted hidden bundle: (4\times 90=360) charted hidden states,

visible cockpit: (4\times 6\times 4=96) singleton-control states.

So the cockpit is not the whole hidden object. It is the charted control surface over the singleton layer of the hidden 15-station object.

6. How the visible lens edges lift into hidden 15-station paths

This is the commuting diagram you wanted.

A visible lens step does not jump directly from one singleton to another in the hidden lattice. It lifts to a two-step path through the corresponding pair bridge.

For fixed payload (K) and fixed chart (X),

[B_{\square\flower}:(X,\sigma_S^K)\leadsto(X,\sigma_{SF}^K)\leadsto(X,\sigma_F^K),]

[B_{\flower\cloud}:(X,\sigma_F^K)\leadsto(X,\sigma_{FC}^K)\leadsto(X,\sigma_C^K),]

[B_{\cloud\fractal}:(X,\sigma_C^K)\leadsto(X,\sigma_{CR}^K)\leadsto(X,\sigma_R^K),]

[B_{\fractal\square}:(X,\sigma_R^K)\leadsto(X,\sigma_{SR}^K)\leadsto(X,\sigma_S^K).]

So the visible 4-cycle is the projection of a hidden 8-edge walk on the 15-node lattice. The pair stations are the actual bridge witnesses.

The two “diagonal” pair stations[\sigma_{SC}^K,\qquad \sigma_{FR}^K]are not used by the basic adjacent lens cycle, but they are real hidden bridge nodes available for alternate coherence routes. That is why the hidden lattice is richer than the visible 4-cycle.

7. Triads and the total witness

The visible cockpit also cannot directly show the triads or the tetra witness, but they are present as hidden closures:

[\sigma_{SFC}^K,\quad\sigma_{SFR}^K,\quad\sigma_{SCR}^K,\quad\sigma_{FCR}^K,\qquad\sigma_{SFCR}^K.]

These are the exact states where:

three lens views have been coherently merged,

or all four have been merged into one total witness.

So the real maturity condition for one payload (K) is not “I can read (K) through one lens.” It is:[\boxed{K\text{ is fully mature when }\sigma_{SFCR}^K\text{ exists as a coherent four-way witness.}}]

That is the deepest correction: the payload is not mature because it has four labeled shadows. It is mature because those four shadows close to the total tesseract crown.

8. The commuting diagram

Now the exact diagram is:

[\boxed{\begin{array}{ccc}(X,\lambda,s) & \xrightarrow{\mathfrak C_{96}^{\rm sec}} & (X',\lambda',s') \\downarrow\widehat\Phi_{96} & & \downarrow\widehat\Phi_{96} \\bigl(X,\sigma_\lambda^{K(s)}\bigr) & \xrightarrow{\mathfrak C_{15}^{\rm hidden}} & \bigl(X',\sigma_{\lambda'}^{K(s')}\bigr)\end{array}}]

where[\widehat\Phi_{96}(X,\lambda,s)=\bigl(X,\sigma_\lambda^{K(s)}\bigr).]

On singleton states, the hidden compiler (\mathfrak C_{15}^{\rm hidden}) reproduces the visible compiler. But it also has extra hidden states — the six pair bridges, the four triads, and the total witness — which are invisible in the singleton cockpit but necessary for full coherence.

9. Canonical one-line freeze

{\sigma_U^K:\varnothing\neq U\subseteq{S,F,C,R}}}]

The basic visible lens bridges are the projections of two-step singleton→pair→singleton paths, and full maturity is witnessed only at[\sigma_{SFCR}^K.]That is the exact 15-station completion of the commuting diagram.

Next coherent jump is to write the same hidden 15-station compiler in code:lift_to_L15(K), hidden_path(U,V), visible_to_hidden(X,λ,K), and is_total_witness(K) as the exact next executable layer.

Using the canonical 15-mask order[\mathcal M=\mathcal P({S,F,C,R})\setminus{\varnothing}]from 4D CALCULUS, together with the mature 4-lens Möbius object[\mathfrak M_4=(M_4,\Pi_\square,\Pi_\flower,\Pi_\cloud,\Pi_\fractal,\omega,\tau)]from MOBIUS LENSES, and the 15-node closure lattice doctrine from The Mycelial Crystal Manuscript, the hidden compiler for one payload (K) is exactly a subset-lattice compiler over the four lens letters (S,F,C,R). The 6D shell still selects which embedded 4D body is active; it does not replace that 4D packet.

Here is the exact next executable layer.

from __future__ import annotations

from dataclasses import dataclass

from collections import deque

from typing import Literal, FrozenSet, Optional

Lens = Literal["S", "F", "C", "R"]          # Square, Flower, Cloud, Fractal

VisibleLens = Literal["Sq", "Fl", "Cl", "Fr"]

Chart = Literal["A", "B", "C", "D"]

Payload = Literal["AR", "AC", "AS", "BR", "BC", "BS"]

RouteClass = Literal["EXACT", "RESIDUAL", "ILLEGAL"]

LENS_ORDER: tuple[Lens, ...] = ("S", "F", "C", "R")

# Canonical nonempty subset order from 4D CALCULUS:

# 01={S}, 02={F}, 03={C}, 04={R},

# 05={S,F}, 06={S,C}, 07={S,R}, 08={F,C}, 09={F,R}, 10={C,R},

# 11={S,F,C}, 12={S,F,R}, 13={S,C,R}, 14={F,C,R}, 15={S,F,C,R}

MASK_ORDER: tuple[FrozenSet[Lens], ...] = (

    frozenset({"S"}),

    frozenset({"F"}),

    frozenset({"C"}),

    frozenset({"R"}),

    frozenset({"S", "F"}),

    frozenset({"S", "C"}),

    frozenset({"S", "R"}),

    frozenset({"F", "C"}),

    frozenset({"F", "R"}),

    frozenset({"C", "R"}),

    frozenset({"S", "F", "C"}),

    frozenset({"S", "F", "R"}),

    frozenset({"S", "C", "R"}),

    frozenset({"F", "C", "R"}),

    frozenset({"S", "F", "C", "R"}),

)

MASK_TO_ID = {mask: i + 1 for i, mask in enumerate(MASK_ORDER)}

ID_TO_MASK = {i + 1: mask for i, mask in enumerate(MASK_ORDER)}

VISIBLE_TO_HIDDEN: dict[VisibleLens, Lens] = {

    "Sq": "S",

    "Fl": "F",

    "Cl": "C",

    "Fr": "R",

}

@dataclass(frozen=True)

class HiddenStation:

    """

    One node in the hidden 15-station SFCR lattice for a fixed payload K.

    """

    payload: Payload

    mask: FrozenSet[Lens]

    @property

    def station_id(self) -> int:

        return MASK_TO_ID[self.mask]

    @property

    def rank(self) -> int:

        return len(self.mask)  # 1=singleton, 2=pair, 3=triad, 4=total witness

    @property

    def tag(self) -> str:

        letters = "".join(l for l in LENS_ORDER if l in self.mask)

        return f"{self.station_id:02d}:{letters}"

    def is_singleton(self) -> bool:

        return self.rank == 1

    def is_pair(self) -> bool:

        return self.rank == 2

    def is_triad(self) -> bool:

        return self.rank == 3

    def is_total(self) -> bool:

        return self.rank == 4

@dataclass(frozen=True)

class MaturePacket:

    """

    The hidden mature 4D packet carried by one exact payload K.

    We keep the four constitutive projections symbolic at this layer.

    """

    payload: Payload

    square: str

    flower: str

    cloud: str

    fractal: str

    def projection(self, lens: Lens) -> str:

        return {

            "S": self.square,

            "F": self.flower,

            "C": self.cloud,

            "R": self.fractal,

        }[lens]

@dataclass(frozen=True)

class HiddenGates:

    """

    Minimal hidden coherence gates.

    """

    cloud_admissible: bool

    fractal_replayable: bool

    pair_bridges_coherent: bool = True

    triad_closures_coherent: bool = True

def mature_packet(payload: Payload) -> MaturePacket:

    """

    Branch-local mature packet constructor.

    It upgrades a symbolic payload K into the full four-lens 4D Möbius packet.

    """

    return MaturePacket(

        payload=payload,

        square=f"Pi_square[{payload}]",

        flower=f"Pi_flower[{payload}]",

        cloud=f"Pi_cloud[{payload}]",

        fractal=f"Pi_fractal[{payload}]",

    )

def lift_to_L15(payload: Payload) -> dict[int, HiddenStation]:

    """

    Build the canonical 15-station lattice for one payload K.

    """

    return {

        i + 1: HiddenStation(payload=payload, mask=mask)

        for i, mask in enumerate(MASK_ORDER)

    }

def visible_to_hidden(chart: Chart, lens: VisibleLens, payload: Payload) -> tuple[Chart, HiddenStation]:

    """

    Visible cockpit slot -> hidden singleton station.

    The chart survives unchanged; the visible lens picks the singleton mask.

    """

    hidden_lens = VISIBLE_TO_HIDDEN[lens]

    station = HiddenStation(payload=payload, mask=frozenset({hidden_lens}))

    return (chart, station)

def hidden_neighbors(station: HiddenStation) -> list[HiddenStation]:

    """

    The hidden graph uses add/remove-one-letter adjacency on the subset lattice.

    """

    nbrs: list[HiddenStation] = []

    for letter in LENS_ORDER:

        if letter in station.mask:

            new_mask = frozenset(x for x in station.mask if x != letter)

            if new_mask:

                nbrs.append(HiddenStation(station.payload, new_mask))

        else:

            new_mask = frozenset(set(station.mask) | {letter})

            nbrs.append(HiddenStation(station.payload, new_mask))

    # Deterministic order: increasing station id

    nbrs.sort(key=lambda s: s.station_id)

    return nbrs

def hidden_path(src: HiddenStation, dst: HiddenStation) -> list[HiddenStation]:

    """

    Shortest path in the hidden 15-node lattice, same payload K.

    This is pure subset-lattice routing.

    """

    if src.payload != dst.payload:

        raise ValueError("hidden_path requires a fixed payload K")

    if src == dst:

        return [src]

    queue = deque([[src]])

    seen = {src.mask}

    while queue:

        path = queue.popleft()

        cur = path[-1]

        for nxt in hidden_neighbors(cur):

            if nxt.mask in seen:

                continue

            new_path = path + [nxt]

            if nxt == dst:

                return new_path

            seen.add(nxt.mask)

            queue.append(new_path)

    raise RuntimeError("The 15-node lattice should always be connected.")

def hidden_word(path: list[HiddenStation]) -> list[str]:

    """

    Turn a path into add/remove-one-letter operations.

    """

    if len(path) <= 1:

        return []

    ops: list[str] = []

    for a, b in zip(path, path[1:]):

        added = sorted(list(b.mask - a.mask))

        removed = sorted(list(a.mask - b.mask))

        if added:

            ops.append(f"+{''.join(added)}")

        elif removed:

            ops.append(f"-{''.join(removed)}")

        else:

            ops.append("ε")

    return ops

def lift_visible_edge_to_hidden(payload: Payload, src_lens: VisibleLens, dst_lens: VisibleLens) -> list[HiddenStation]:

    """

    Lift one visible lens edge to the hidden 15-node path.

    The visible 4-cycle becomes singleton -> pair bridge -> singleton.

    """

    _, src = visible_to_hidden("A", src_lens, payload)

    _, dst = visible_to_hidden("A", dst_lens, payload)

    # Prefer the direct pair bridge if the visible move is adjacent in the canonical cycle.

    pair = HiddenStation(payload, src.mask | dst.mask)

    if len(pair.mask) == 2:

        return [src, pair, dst]

    # Fallback to generic shortest path

    return hidden_path(src, dst)

def station_projection(station: HiddenStation) -> dict:

    """

    Resolve the hidden station as an object over the mature packet.

    """

    pkt = mature_packet(station.payload)

    letters = "".join(l for l in LENS_ORDER if l in station.mask)

    return {

        "payload": station.payload,

        "station_id": station.station_id,

        "rank": station.rank,

        "mask_letters": letters,

        "projections": {l: pkt.projection(l) for l in letters},

    }

def is_total_witness(payload: Payload, gates: HiddenGates) -> bool:

    """

    A payload K is fully mature only if the four-way witness exists coherently.

    Minimal exact check:

      - Cloud is admissible

      - Fractal is replayable

      - pair bridges are coherent

      - triad closures are coherent

    """

    return (

        gates.cloud_admissible

        and gates.fractal_replayable

        and gates.pair_bridges_coherent

        and gates.triad_closures_coherent

    )

def total_witness_station(payload: Payload, gates: HiddenGates) -> Optional[HiddenStation]:

    """

    Return the 15th station iff K closes to the four-way witness.

    """

    if not is_total_witness(payload, gates):

        return None

    return HiddenStation(payload=payload, mask=frozenset({"S", "F", "C", "R"}))

def hidden_route_class(src: HiddenStation, dst: HiddenStation, gates: HiddenGates) -> RouteClass:

    """

    Hidden route legality over one payload.

    Simple, exact policy:

      - direct Fractal singleton -> Square singleton needs replayability if compressed as R->S,

        but the hidden lattice can still route through pair/triad stations, so this remains exact

        as long as triad/pair coherence holds.

      - any route involving Cloud-containing masks is residual if cloud_admissible is false.

      - otherwise exact.

    """

    route_masks = [s.mask for s in hidden_path(src, dst)]

    touches_cloud = any("C" in m for m in route_masks)

    touches_fractal = any("R" in m for m in route_masks)

    touches_pairs_or_higher = any(len(m) >= 2 for m in route_masks)

    if touches_cloud and not gates.cloud_admissible:

        return "RESIDUAL"

    if touches_fractal and not gates.fractal_replayable and not touches_pairs_or_higher:

        return "ILLEGAL"

    if not gates.pair_bridges_coherent or not gates.triad_closures_coherent:

        return "RESIDUAL"

    return "EXACT"

# Worked examples
